Alexander Grothendieck, one of the great eccentric geniuses of 20th century mathematics, has died in France at the age of 86 on November 14, 2014. The maths master reached the very pinnacle of his profession before abandoning the discipline, taking up anti-war activism, retreating into the life of a recluse and refusing to share his research. Grothendieck went on to become a revolutionary mathematician, doing groundbreaking work on algebra and geometry that won him the Fields medal, known as the Nobel prize of the maths world, in 1966.
